# Task: Refactor Roslyn Symbol Lookup to Unified Resolution Strategy

## Background
Roslyn's symbol lookup has separate code paths for different contexts (expression binding, type resolution, member access). This task extracts common patterns into a shared strategy.

## Objective
Create a `UnifiedSymbolResolver` that consolidates the common symbol lookup patterns used across different binding contexts.

## Steps
1. Study symbol resolution in `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/`
2. Identify common patterns in `Binder.LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder`, `Binder_Lookup.cs`, and type resolution
3. Create `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs` with:
   - A strategy interface `ISymbolResolutionStrategy`
   - Concrete strategies for: TypeResolution, MemberAccess, NamespaceResolution
   - A `Resolve()` method that walks scope chains using the strategy
   - Results type that captures both found symbols and diagnostics
4. Create a test file in the test directory

## Key Reference Files
- `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder_Lookup.cs`
- `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Binder.cs`
- `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Symbols/` — symbol types

## Success Criteria
- UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs exists
- Defines ISymbolResolutionStrategy interface
- Has concrete strategy implementations
- Test file exists

I am thinking...: Now I have a thorough understanding of the codebase. Let me plan the implementation:

## What to build

### `UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs`

This file needs:
1. `ISymbolResolutionStrategy` interface - a strategy for resolving symbols
2. Three concrete strategy implementations:
   - `TypeResolutionStrategy` - resolves type symbols using `LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly`
   - `MemberAccessResolutionStrategy` - resolves member access using `LookupMembersInternal`
   - `NamespaceResolutionStrategy` - resolves namespace symbols using namespace-focused options
3. `UnifiedSymbolResolver` class with a `Resolve()` method that accepts a strategy

### Design decisions:

**ISymbolResolutionStrategy interface:**
```csharp
internal interface ISymbolResolutionStrategy
{
    void Resolve(Binder binder, LookupResult result, string name, int arity,
                 ConsList<TypeSymbol> basesBeingResolved, bool diagnose,
                 ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol> useSiteInfo);
}
```

**UnifiedSymbolResolver class:**
The `Resolve()` method should:
- Take a `Binder`, a `string name`, `int arity`, and an `ISymbolResolutionStrategy`
- Allocate a `LookupResult` from the pool
- Call the strategy's Resolve method
- Return the symbols found
- Free the LookupResult

**TypeResolutionStrategy:**
- Uses `LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly`
- Calls `binder.LookupSymbolsInSingleBinder` or the binder chain approach

**MemberAccessResolutionStrategy:**
- Needs a `NamespaceOrTypeSymbol` qualifier
- Calls `LookupMembersInternal` on the binder

**NamespaceResolutionStrategy:**
- Uses `LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly` but focuses on namespaces only
- Could filter to only namespace symbols

Let me look at how to structure this carefully. The key insight from studying `Looku

Running command: cd /workspace && git add src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs src/Compilers/CSharp/Test/Symbol/Compilation/UnifiedSymbolResolverTests.cs && git commit -m "Add UnifiedSymbolResolver with strategy pattern and tests

Introduces symbol-resolution infrastructure in the CSharp binder layer:

- ISymbolResolutionStrategy (internal interface) — single Resolve() method
  taking Binder, LookupResult, name, arity, basesBeingResolved, diagnose,
  and ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol>.

- TypeResolutionStrategy — resolves named types via scope-chain walk
  (LookupSymbolsSimpleName with NamespacesOrTypesOnly, qualifierOpt: null).

- MemberAccessResolutionStrategy — resolves members of an explicit
  NamespaceOrTypeSymbol qualifier (LookupOptions.Default).
  Throws ArgumentNullException when qualifier is null.

- NamespaceResolutionStrategy — resolves namespaces via scope-chain walk;
  post-filters result to exclude any type symbols that share the name.

- UnifiedSymbolResolver — composes a Binder with an
  ISymbolResolutionStrategy.  Resolve() borrows a pooled LookupResult,
  invokes the strategy, and returns an ImmutableArray<Symbol> (or Empty).
  Throws ArgumentNullException for null binder/name/strategy.

Test file (Microsoft.CodeAnalysis.CSharp.Symbol.UnitTests):
- 12 [Fact] tests in UnifiedSymbolResolverTests : CSharpTestBase
- Null-guard tests for all three public constructors / entry-points
- Functional tests for each strategy: type-by-name, namespace-by-name,
  namespace/type disambiguation (RemoveAll filter), member-of-namespace,
  field-of-type, and empty-result cases
- Binder obtained via CSharpSemanticModel.GetEnclosingBinder(position)
  at a source-marker position, matching existing test conventions

Co-authored-by: openhands

## What was built

### `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs`

| Type | Role |
|---|---|
| `ISymbolResolutionStrategy` | Internal interface — one `Resolve()` method whose signature exactly matches the internal Roslyn binder contract (`ref CompoundUseSiteInfo<AssemblySymbol>`, `ConsList<TypeSymbol>`, etc.) |
| `TypeResolutionStrategy` | Calls `Binder.LookupSymbolsSimpleName` with `qualifierOpt: null` and `LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly` — finds types reachable through the enclosing scope chain |
| `MemberAccessResolutionStrategy` | Calls `LookupSymbolsSimpleName` with an explicit `NamespaceOrTypeSymbol` qualifier and `LookupOptions.Default` — finds declared members of a specific container; throws `ArgumentNullException` when the qualifier is `null` |
| `NamespaceResolutionStrategy` | Same scope-chain walk as `TypeResolutionStrategy`, then calls `result.Symbols.RemoveAll(s => s.Kind != SymbolKind.Namespace)` to discard any type symbols that share the name |
| `UnifiedSymbolResolver` | Composes a `Binder` with an `ISymbolResolutionStrategy`; `Resolve()` borrows a pooled `LookupResult` in a `try/finally` (so `Free()` is always called), invokes the strategy, and returns `ImmutableArray<Symbol>` (or `Empty`) |

An error is attached with the inaccessibility errors. Non-accessible results take priority over\n    ///                      non-viable results.\n    ///    a non-viable result - a result that means that the search continues into further scopes of lower priority for\n    ///                          a viable or non-accessible result. An error is attached with the error that indicates\n    ///                          why the result is non-viable. "// Licensed to the .NET Foundation under one or more agreements.\n// The .NET Foundation licenses this file to you under the MIT license.\n// See the LICENSE file in the project root for more information.\n\n#nullable disable\n\nusing System.Diagnostics;\nusing Microsoft.CodeAnalysis.CSharp.Symbols;\nusing Microsoft.CodeAnalysis.CSharp.Syntax;\nusing Microsoft.CodeAnalysis.Text;\nusing Roslyn.Utilities;\n\nnamespace Microsoft.CodeAnalysis.CSharp\n{\n    /// <summary>\n    /// Classifies the different ways in which a found symbol might be incorrect.\n    /// Higher values are considered \"better\" than lower values. These values are used\n    /// in a few different places:\n    ///    1) Inside a LookupResult to indicate the quality of a symbol from lookup.\n    ///    2) Inside a bound node (for example, BoundBadExpression), to indicate\n    ///       the \"binding quality\" of the symbols referenced by that bound node.\n    ///    3) Inside an error type symbol, to indicate the reason that the candidate symbols\n    ///       in the error type symbols were not good.\n    ///\n    /// While most of the values can occur in all places, some of the problems are not\n    /// detected at lookup time (e.g., NotAVariable), so only occur in bound nodes.\n    /// </summary>\n    /// <remarks>\n    /// This enumeration is parallel to and almost the same as the CandidateReason enumeration.\n    /// Changes to one should usually result in changes to the other.\n    ///\n    /// There are two enumerations because:\n    ///   1) CandidateReason in language-independent, while this enum is language specific.\n    ///   2) The name \"CandidateReason\" didn't make much sense in the way LookupResultKind is used internally.\n    ///   3) Viable isn't used in CandidateReason, but we need it in LookupResultKind, and there isn't a\n    ///      a way to have internal enumeration values.\n    /// </remarks>\n    internal enum LookupResultKind : byte\n    {\n        // Note: order is important! High values take precedences over lower values.\n\n        Empty,\n        NotATypeOrNamespace,\n        NotAnAttributeType,\n        WrongArity,\n        NotCreatable,      // E.g., new of an interface or static class\n        Inaccessible,\n        NotReferencable,   // E.g., get_Goo binding to an accessor.\n        NotAValue,\n        NotAVariable,      // used for several slightly different places, e.g. LHS of =, out/ref parameters, etc.\n        NotInvocable,\n        NotLabel,          // used when a label is required\n        StaticInstanceMismatch,\n        OverloadResolutionFailure,\n\n        // Note: within LookupResult, LookupResultKind.Ambiguous is currently not used (in C#). Instead\n        // ambiguous results are determined later by examining multiple viable results to determine if\n        // they are ambiguous or overloaded. Thus, LookupResultKind.Ambiguous does not occur in a LookupResult,\n        // but can occur within a BoundBadExpression.\n        Ambiguous,\n\n        // Indicates a set of symbols, and they are totally fine.\n        MemberGroup,\n\n        // Indicates a single symbol is totally fine.\n        Viable,\n    }\n\n    internal static class LookupResultKindExtensions\n    {\n        /// <summary>\n        /// Maps a LookupResultKind to a CandidateReason.
